  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c4562758-d9d9-49c9-88ea-eb04e815705a'

Expected publication is June 2nd 2020 according to Harper Collins Children’s Books ;)

</script>    </div>

<div id="review_2989967993" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2989967993" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52930632-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554853474p2/52930632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2989967993?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/52930632-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/50895084-one-true-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=what-is-this-sorcery">what-is-this-sorcery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=i-will-read-anything-by-this-author">i-will-read-anything-by-this-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=hyped-af-to-read">hyped-af-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=teamwork-makes-the-dream-work">teamwork-makes-the-dream-work</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=illustrated">illustrated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2989967993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3739760239423259093"><blockquote>
  <i>In her years at school, Good and Evil played by the rules.<br/>But in the Camelot years? Play by the rules and you die.</i>
</blockquote><p><b>It's rare to find a series conclusion that feels as perfect as 'One True King' did.</b> This was a wonderful way to close out one of my all-time favourite series! <b>It's explosive, touching, hilarious, maddeningly stressful yet fulfilling at the same time.</b></p><p><b>I was amazed at how much information - plot, backstory, character development - was packed into these 500-ish pages.</b> No words were w</p></span>
  <span id="freeText3739760239423259093" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>In her years at school, Good and Evil played by the rules.<br>But in the Camelot years? Play by the rules and you die.</i>
</blockquote><p><b>It's rare to find a series conclusion that feels as perfect as 'One True King' did.</b> This was a wonderful way to close out one of my all-time favourite series! <b>It's explosive, touching, hilarious, maddeningly stressful yet fulfilling at the same time.</b></p><p><b>I was amazed at how much information - plot, backstory, character development - was packed into these 500-ish pages.</b> No words were wasted, nor did any scene feel unnecessary!</p><blockquote>
  <i>Tedros had his plan.<br>But everyone has a plan until they’re kicked in the face.<br> Then the plan isn’t worth very much, is it?</i>
</blockquote><p><b>There were <i>so</i> many twists, cliffhanger chapter endings and edge-of-my-seat moments</b> - OTK was exhilarating and exhausting in the best way. <b>The multiple open plot threads wove together into an intricate web, a complex endgame that blew my mind.</b> Small details in previous books suddenly become significant in new light and I hardly knew what to expect.</p><blockquote>
  <i>Past is Present and Present is Past. The story goes round and round again...Unless you learn from that past.</i>
</blockquote><p><b>I'm so proud of how far our protagonists have come from their Book 1 selves.</b> Spending the past five years with them has been a blessing! <b>I'm especially proud and protective of Tedros</b>, the once-King of Camelot and son of Arthur, vying to reclaim and truly earn his throne. <b>We see his deepest vulnerabilities, his growth in wisdom, courage and confidence, yet he retains his classic Tedrosian air of mild confusion.</b></p><blockquote>
  <i>"Tell me [Tedros]. Why do you want to die and come back to life?”<br>...He thought about this awhile...“Because if I can die and come back to life, then no one can hurt me.”</i>
</blockquote><p>I'm not joking when I say I would die for this kid.</p><p><b>Agatha and Sophie also show significant development</b>, Agatha in learning how to cede control and Sophie in finally understanding why she's never felt fulfilled. <b>The personalities of other characters like Hort, Anadil and Reena also become much more fleshed-out.</b> Of course, given the huge collection of characters in this book (actually Books 4-6 as a whole), most attention is given to the major players but there's definitely enough material for spin-offs with minor characters (*looks at Soman hopefully*). <b>The adult characters also play important roles and have nuanced personalities, which is refreshing to see in YA.</b> While pretty much all of them made questionable decisions in the past (that their kids are now ensnared by), the adults really do try to make amends and help their children, both Good and Evil! <b>Speaking of Evil...Japeth is so loathsome.</b></p><blockquote>
  <i>“Girls have a stink that can’t scrub off. Aric had a good way of describing it. Like a rose gone to rot. I can smell it anywhere. But you...I’m afraid you reek of it worst of all.”</i>
</blockquote><p>Because that's not creepy at all! Some villains I like or at least respect on some level, but not Japeth. <b>Cheating, gaslighting, scum of the earth.</b></p><p><b>The aforementioned character development is what makes the romance in this book so convincing.</b> Tedros and Agatha really grow together as a team, especially at the end, and though I have always shipped them, in OTK it feels like their relationship grows deeper and more mature. (Not sexually, I mean... wiser? More understanding of each others' whole selves.)</p><blockquote>
  <i>“If anything happens to me, don’t mourn for me...You’re to go on. You’re to keep fighting. You’re to do what needs to be done. Don’t let what happens to me stop us from getting to The End. I’m with you in life and death.”</i>
</blockquote><p><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429212913ra/14550321.gif" width="400" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>^ Me refusing to consider the possibility of a major character death. There were many moments of hysterical laughing in denial!</p><p><b>Two other major, fan-favourite (I think?) ships also bloomed, and I'm so thankful they felt natural and not like fan-service.</b> I won't elaborate too much as I don't want to spoil, but I'm really happy that both parties in Sophie's pairing did a lot of growing before finally getting together. Being comfortable alone and knowing yourself and what you want are important in a relationship! (Speaking as someone with zero experience, hah!) <b>It's oddly fitting that the queer relationships in the Endless Woods are finally being canonically realised during Pride Month.</b> There aren't labels in the Woods (which Soman has purposefully left vague) but it's clear that same-sex relationships are recognised and there was also a brief discussion of gender fluidity! <b>I was particularly happy about Tedros' bisexuality/pansexuality</b>, as it's been fanon since Book 2 and finally, finally we've been validated.</p><p>
  <b>The friendships were also a highlight of this book, especially that between the witches of the Coven.</b>
</p><blockquote>
  <i>“You’re my real family, you know,” Dot said softly to her friends. “And I know I’m a part of yours too. Even if you act like I’m not. Even if you two pretend you don’t need me. A coven is three. It has to be three. Because I’d be so lonely without you.”</i>
</blockquote><p>Oh my heart. Absolute girl gang goals. <b>I also loved the reaffirmation of the Sophie-Agatha friendship, and other characters growing out of earlier childish jealousies.</b> This truly feels like a coming-of-age novel!</p><p><b>In classic SGE style, OTK offers some apt social commentary and general life lessons.</b> The concept about how <b>fate and free will must operate in tandem</b> is particularly insightful - life really does test us and builds us into who we are.</p><blockquote>
  <i>We are all objects of our fate, but our will decides whether we overcome the challenges fate brings us. The Storian only begins our tale. We must end it.</i>
</blockquote> I also loved how it stresses that <b>kingship isn't through blood, the right to govern is earned, and that no leader should reign forever. Owning up to your mistakes rather than seeking to blame or deny, and using your regrets to move forward</b> is another important message. <blockquote>
  <i>At some point, people become afraid of life’s mysteries. With age, their lives get smaller and smaller. They judge with their fears instead of their hearts. In your world, not everyone can have a happy ending. The Pen won’t allow it. But in my world, every Man thinks they deserve one. They turn on each other when things go wrong. They try to beat back the hand of fate. And when they can’t...that’s when Evil is born. Real Evil.</i>
</blockquote><p><b>Upon finishing this book, I was both happy and heartbroken.</b> Joyous because of what an amazing ending SGE was given, but devastated that this was The End. <b>I suppose the only remedy is a re-read soon...</b></p><blockquote>
  <i>“The End of Ends...the stories told...What wondrous souls you are.”</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3739760239423259093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2912882857?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ramona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ramona" href="/user/show/52524382-ramona">Ramona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/53828515-one-true-king">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2912882857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17870442801364109786">Oh boy. So.<br/><br/>Lots of mixed feelings about this book, as well as this second trilogy as a whole. Essentially it boils down to occasionally nice moments mixed in with mess.<br/><br/>I really have to go into spoilers to get into the meat of my opinions, so from here on out you've been warned, my dears.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[So, I was not thrilled with the treatment of Agatha in relation to Tedros and his quest to be king. I haven't been for the entirety of this trilogy, if my previous reviews give any indication. This</span></span>
  <span id="freeText17870442801364109786" style="display:none">Oh boy. So.<br><br>Lots of mixed feelings about this book, as well as this second trilogy as a whole. Essentially it boils down to occasionally nice moments mixed in with mess.<br><br>I really have to go into spoilers to get into the meat of my opinions, so from here on out you've been warned, my dears.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, I was not thrilled with the treatment of Agatha in relation to Tedros and his quest to be king. I haven't been for the entirety of this trilogy, if my previous reviews give any indication. This spurned my desire for Agatha to essentially prove herself as a king instead, and Tedros to get off his decidedly-sexist high-horse and accept that her being by his side means sometimes leading the charge, fighting the battle herself, and him being the support instead - because when she takes charge? Shit more religiously gets done.<br><br>Practically every expectation that is put on Agatha to be a proper princess/queen is compromising who she is fundamentally as a person, and I am not a fan. There's a difference between letting someone work through what they need to work through on their own and supporting from the side, and sitting by while they continue to put themselves and others in jeopardy, and quite frankly I was sick of everyone jumping down Agatha's throat when she (in my opinion) is rightly doing the latter when it comes to her thick-headed boyfriend.<br><br>The image of Agatha tied up while Tedros faced Japeth all on his own is just how I picture their relationship as a whole now, I can't help it. Sorry. They can be cute all they want, but it's clear to me that they might not be as equal as they say they are.<br><br>Speaking of Tedros (ugh), dare I say there was too much of him in this book, and I'm not just saying that as someone who isn't his biggest fan. In the previous two books, we were given so many characters' perspectives, reading about people doing things all over the place! Now the focus, I feel, remains too much on what needs to be done for Tedros and everyone focusing on Tedros. It was that instead of characters focusing on stopping Rhian and Japeth, the Terrible Twins Two: Electric Boogaloo, while also having their own character journies alongside this. It's like, Nicola? Irrelevant. Beatrix, Kiko, and Reena? Reena can have <i>some</i> backstory, but let's sideline the other two except to provide commentary occasionally. The Coven? Give 'em a couple of chapters and confirm Hesterdil. Hort? Even I missed his perspectives; at least it was <i>different</i>. Agatha and Sophie? Their glorious blazes snuffed into the bare flicker of a flame. And Tedros' "development" itself seems to happen in a snap, almost as if by magic... there's no steady development. It's all at once, and I'm not a fan again. Honestly, so was Agatha and Sophie's "development"; out of the three, Sophie's was the best, but that's not saying much. It all felt <i>rushed</i>.<br><br>Continuing on with the other characters, I feel like there was so much lost potential with Japeth. Him being an actual complex character was set up pretty well last book, but here he was just a one-note evil villain type. And that's it. Nothing else. Even his relationship with Aric amounted to barely anything. He's just bad and we have to hate and kill him. The scenes where his memories are viewed aren't even about <i>him</i>; they just confirm his and his brother's true origins, SPEAKING OF WHICH...<br><br>What? <i>What???</i> The School Master's sons. The. School. Master's. Sons. The same School Master who <i>rejected</i> Evelyn Sader and her love. I honestly don't know what else to say other than "WHAT?!"<br><br>After <i>that</i> reveal, I read with <i>such</i> a decrease in enthusiasm, just waiting for this to be <i>o-ver</i>.<br><br>And <i>Chaddick</i> being Tedros' brother and the son of Lady Gremlaine and Arthur? Felt hollow, because Chaddick didn't have much of a significant character beforehand. He was Tedros' bestie and a solid knight, but from what I recall, we didn't fully get to know him as a person before he died because he was never a majorly developed character. <br><br>Continuing on with relationships that made me go "WHAT?!", Hort and Sophie is literally one of the most unsavory romances I think I've ever read, with it trying to masquerade as a great love story for the ages but, with their history that's just plain toxic and involving a whole lot of obsession, is just... off. <i>No</i> thank you.<br><br>So here's more of a critique of the whole trilogy, something which is really starting to grate on me now: the lack of set-up for so many of the major plot points. In this book, what stood out to me the most were the three tests and their out-of-nowhere significance to Tedros, as well as to King Arthur and Merlin. Honestly even the whole Lion and Snake thing felt out of left field from the start. I can tell that I'm supposed to take everything seriously, but I just can't help but think about the original trilogy, and how <i>NONE OF THIS</i> was brought up or even hinted at. If any of y'all can correct me on this and comment on something that actually was hinted on in the first three books, please hit me up and I'd love to discuss. But for me at the moment, it really drives home the feeling that the second trilogy wasn't originally meant to be, and whether that fact is true or not, it makes it more in your face that it's a possibility from a writing standpoint. Basically there's a feeling of "let's throw things at the wall and see what sticks" rather than a naturally flowing progression from Book 1 to Book 6.<br><br>Um... so... positives of <u>One True King</u>!<br><br>• Agatha. No matter what nonsense is thrown her way. Point blank period.<br>• I finally like Sophie; in fact, I wanted to see more of her in this book.<br>• Agatha and Sophie's friendship is sugary sweet, I've come to adore it. I'm kinda disappointed that it became less of a focal point over time, substituted for more <i>Tedros</i>.<br>• Merlin. His death really stung, he truly was a champ.<br>• The Coven.<br>• Willam/Bogden and Hesterdil.<br>• The fact that Agatha was technically a king for .2 seconds.<br>• *through gritted teeth* Tedros'... proposal... was actually... very beautiful...<br>• The ending felt like things were truly ending.<br><br>Seriously, please let this series end now. I truly think it's time to stop. No sequel series about characters' kids or something; it wouldn't even feel the same and feel more like dragging this out simply for nostalgia or profit. I'd really love to read something new from Chainani, because although I have criticized he seems like a really creative guy with a lot of ideas in his noggin.<br><br>So I encourage:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505855007ra/23965262.gif" width="498" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1747491939" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of <u>Quests for Glory</u></a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2147274256" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of <u>A Crystal of Time</u></a><br><br>•••••••••<br><br><b>PRE-READ EDIT 4/15/2020:</b><br><br>I'm so glad I caught the <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UfA51kZIRq4" rel="nofollow noopener">book trailer</a> only a day after it was released so I wasn't the last to the party.<br><br>There's not much to comment on, honestly, as the trailer didn't really give anything away. Probably because it's the very last book (or is it? Because we thought <u>The Last Ever After</u> was, literally, the last "ever after" and...) and everything will only be revealed within the pages. Anyway. I'll say it again, probably for the last time until June 2nd: Let's. Do. This. <br><br>•••••••••<br><br><b>PRE-READ EDIT 11/1/19:</b><br><br>I actually saw the cover a while ago, but now I finally have a moment to comment on it.<br><br>It's definitely got a different vibe than the other covers this series has had, but I don't think it's bad. I'm here for it, and honestly, Tedros looks the best he ever has on a cover (and no, it's not just because he's not prominent haha). Again, let's do this.<br><br>As for the <a href="https://ew.com/books/2019/10/08/one-true-king-school-good-evil-final-book-preview/" rel="nofollow noopener">preview</a>, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it seems our Sophie isn't quite herself... and yet, at the same time, she is. Looks like Agatha's gonna have to set her head straight again, and make her remember that she had friends and character development last book. Also I get the feeling that Kei's gonna turn to Team Tedros (but, really, let's be honest, it's Team Agatha). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>•••••••••<br><br><b>PRE-READ EDIT 8/23/19:</b><br><br>And so we have our title... <u>One True King</u>. It fits. It works. I’m feelin’ it. Let’s do this.<br><br>Tedros still has yet to evolve from his dingleberry ways, but yeah, let’s do this.<br><br>Plot twist: the “One True King” was Agatha the entire time. If that’s true I’ll cry. #KingAgatha</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_3410949625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3410949625" />
    <a title="Layla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109681904-layla"><img alt="Layla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602279778p2/109681904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3410949625?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Layla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Layla" href="/user/show/109681904-layla">Layla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062695215" href="/book/show/50175196-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3410949625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4817276071499166246"><b>~A surprising 4.25 stars~</b><br/><br/>I can't believe this is the finale. This series is finally over! This book is hands down my favorite out of the the Camelot years. The Quest for Glory was underwhelming, and The Crystal of Time dragged. I'm writing this 3 days after I've finished this because it's finals week :( . I've had time to reflect on it and honestly this one was surprisingly good. I expected the same trend of it being not as engaging enough to continue, but I finished this in 4 days, and I was re</span>
  <span id="freeText4817276071499166246" style="display:none"><b>~A surprising 4.25 stars~</b><br /><br />I can't believe this is the finale. This series is finally over! This book is hands down my favorite out of the the Camelot years. The Quest for Glory was underwhelming, and The Crystal of Time dragged. I'm writing this 3 days after I've finished this because it's finals week :( . I've had time to reflect on it and honestly this one was surprisingly good. I expected the same trend of it being not as engaging enough to continue, but I finished this in 4 days, and I was reading like 2 other books at the same time, which compared how long it took me to read the one before, it's great.<br /><br />I really enjoyed it, and there are so many mysteries solved, and when they were it made so much sense, and everything started to click into place including past hints given that went over my head. The only one that felt abrupt was the mystery of the true heir of Camelot.The hints were there, but the explanation was lackluster. Many ships were also made cannon, including Hophie. I don't know how many times I have to say this, but this relationship is not it. The only thing they both have in common is the fact that they are both insufferable and push away people. Sophie did have character development, where I like her much better than before, but still. Not that I want Hort with Nicola together, because according to my calculations, she's 14, and he's 17 or 18. <br /><br />I also really like the relationship development with Tedros and Agatha, as they started to trust each other more (even if this development happened too quickly) and bickered a lot less because their banter was staring to get annoying and repetitive. But I don't like how it kind of potrayed Agatha as someone who messes up everything and always tries to take control, when in reality, if it wasn't for her, everyone would have been screwed. Tedros (who has a combination of 2 braincells that he was somehow able to combine and do something smart and useful for once) nor any of the other quest member have any right to criticize or doubt her. <br /><br />The other thing I didn't like was that this book did that thing where they just kill off every other side character in the last book, that no longer have any use, for the sake of adding tension. But I litterly felt no sympathy for any of the deaths. They left no impact or importance. Except one, that I'm not going to talk about for the sake of spoilers.<br /><br />I'm sad that this is a wrap on my childhood and the book series I've been following for so many years. I do hope there is a spin off or at least a novella for just The Coven (Hester, Dot of Ani). I know I listed a good amount things I didn't like, but I'm still rating it 4.25, for generousity, nostalgia, and the fact that I enjoyed this more than I expected.<br /><br /><b>here are the reviews for the books previous:</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3404720445" rel="nofollow noopener">The School for Good and Evil: ★★★★ .5</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/3178099642/comments" rel="nofollow noopener">A World Without Princes: ★★★★</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3178099834" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Ever After: ★★★★</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3545270277" rel="nofollow noopener">Quest for Glory:★★★★</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3605564713?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">A Crystal of Time:★★★.5</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2968634773?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/48545994-kate">Kate</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2968634773&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2968634773" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9171866822180394008">Okay my thoughts are fairly coherent now<br/>****BIG SPOILERS:****<br/><br/>I'll start w the negative so we can end on a high:<br/>- Soman get a new plot twist that's doesn't cause beef between the trio challenge <br/>- also Bettina was basically pointless, he really didn't need her at all??   <span id="freeText9171866822180394008" style="display:none">Okay my thoughts are fairly coherent now<br />****BIG SPOILERS:****<br /><br />I'll start w the negative so we can end on a high:<br />- Soman get a new plot twist that's doesn't cause beef between the trio challenge <br />- also Bettina was basically pointless, he really didn't need her at all?? Hm<br />- Willam and Bogden were also pretty much useless <br />- Kei's death was so disappointing, he had so much potential for an interesting character arc but he just. Died<br />- most of the deaths in this were just "eh"-- Kei, Robin Hood, Bettina, Dean Brunhilde, even Guinevere-- <br />- Agatha still felt a bit flat, though not quite as bad as she has done in the past <br />- the Chaddick twist kinda came out of nowhere like,,,, I like that it meant he and Tedros were brothers but I think it would have meant more if he'd been more fleshed out and we knew him better. It was okay.<br />- plot felt too chaotic and weird in places <br />- Hophie. Eye roll, much. It's just personal preference but. Nah. <br />- Nicola got a shitty ending. Rebound K-pop boy boyfriend? Come off it Chainani. She was meant to be important.<br />-UM, NEW SCHOOL MASTER??? NO??? JUST FORGOT ABT THAT DID WE??? Hmph<br /><br />Middling stuff:<br />- I think I liked the Hestadil? I think it's canon? It's canon right?? Not as much as the het couples but I think so<br />- the baby Merlin thing was just weird. It was fine. Idk.<br />- Tedros playing Aric? Eek. Idk. I still have no sympathy for either Japeth or Aric <br /><br />Things I did like:<br />-TEDROOOOOOSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSSS!!!!!!!!! HE FINALLY GOT THE BOOK HE DESERVED! HE HAD THE BRAINCELL! His two plans were brilliant and he did so so so well I love him sooo much. The way he tricked the genie was amazing. He went to his death w dignity and poise, knowing the whole thing relied on Agatha and therefore not sure if he'd get to come back to life BUT IT WORKED. Also I like how he charmed the lady of the lake and tink hah. He got a gnarly scar too.<br />- I felt so bad for him tho like Guinevere didn't even want him to find her????? D: also I hate Arthur now idc what anyone says <br />- that flashback scene w Tedros and Merlin in Ender's forest... Made me cry it was so good <br />- I loved the library scene it was so funny-- Hort's shanty and the senile ("senile") librarian calling them "Agoff and Teedum" lmaoooo<br />- Merlin's death was rly well done :( "my king" reminded me of Boromir's death and "the work is done" is the perfect ending line<br />- Sophie and Tedros's arcs were really top tier. Agatha's was okay but Sophie and Tedros's were just amazing. Legends.<br />- "ALL OF YOU WILL DIE" ugh Sophie I LOVE YOU. plus the red bob lmaooo. And she nearly killed Japeth w that scream HELL YEAH shsjjs<br />-Dot's reaction to the Sheriff's death was rly well done <br />- I rly enjoyed Reena's bit and the stuff with the Knights of Eleven! It was great, so good <br />- I WAS RIGHT ABOUT MAID MARIAN BEING DOT'S MOTHER <br />- Tedros bi confirmed!!!!!! Took you long enough eh Soman <br />- I got king Agatha for a brief second lmaooo <br />- HNNG. WEDDING. I got mild beef w the design of Agatha's wedding dress but I'll put it aside bc I love Tagatha so much<br />- just tagatha in general actually. Agatha trying to get the apple off him coz she was hungry without realising it was important I HAAAATE her 💀💀 love it <br />- whiskey woo reprise<br />- I said I didn't like Hophie but the scene where he tried to find food without all the stuff she wouldn't eat and couldn't find it so he brought pretty cookies instead .. hhh. Good scene for a "meh" ship <br /><br />It was a really good ending to TCY! not on TLEA or SGE level but I would say third in line (SGE, TLEA, OTK, ACOT, AWWP, QFG) and I really did like it. The middle section where the second task began rly made me feel sick w anxiety hhh I won't be rereading that but the rest was rly good! I feel so bad for Rhian tho man. Poor guy really believed it. Japeth was a fairly flat villain but honestly it was bigger than him so I'll let it lie. I'll reread when I have my physical copy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9171866822180394008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4795723609120242299"><b>THAT'S IT. THE END.</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591998727ra/29637811.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591998727ra/29637812.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>THANK YOU SOMAN CHAINANI for this series.</b> I did not appreciate the first book as much when I was younger as I did when I was older. And, had I not reread the first book, I would never have traversed through all the kingdoms, stories, and quests that these six books have taken me.<br/><br/>Soman Chainani has crafted a tale of complex and diverse characters that are flawed in every way, but still living how they are meant to. There are so many details in here to keep track of that while t</span>
  <span id="freeText4795723609120242299" style="display:none"><b>THAT'S IT. THE END.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591998727ra/29637811.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1591998727ra/29637812.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>THANK YOU SOMAN CHAINANI for this series.</b> I did not appreciate the first book as much when I was younger as I did when I was older. And, had I not reread the first book, I would never have traversed through all the kingdoms, stories, and quests that these six books have taken me.<br><br>Soman Chainani has crafted a tale of complex and diverse characters that are flawed in every way, but still living how they are meant to. There are so many details in here to keep track of that while the plot twists might come out of nowhere, if you read back, you realize it's been right in front of you this entire time. And yes, the series is flawed, but it has become one of my favorites. <br><br>Chainani is also able to weave in deep messages of love, gender, sexuality, conformity, redemption, Evil vs. Good, feminism, etc. in such a beautiful way. So much love within theses books. Agatha mentions how love can come in so many forms and I found that beautiful to add. <br><br>The series isn't all happy and it's not all sad, and I love that it is as it is. <blockquote>
  <i>"Camelot might be our Ever After," said Agatha. "But this [the School for Good and Evil] is where our fairy tale began."</i>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3303984767" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3303984767" />
    <a title="ellie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36615677-ellie"><img alt="ellie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603833383p2/36615677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3303984767?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ellie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ellie" href="/user/show/36615677-ellie">ellie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36615677-ellie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36615677-ellie?shelf=made-me-sob">made-me-sob</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3303984767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12570770829585081275">✨ April 27th, 2020 ✨<br/><br/>These books have been so formative to me as a reader, writer, and person for so many years, and it’s surreal to realize that the series ends in just a month and a few days. I’ve grown up hand in hand with these characters— I’ve navigated new school hallways with my paperback carefully tucked in my bag, made my first internet friends in forums on the author’s website, and traveled to my first book conventions in New York City and Charleston because of these stories. Over the y</span>
  <span id="freeText12570770829585081275" style="display:none">✨ April 27th, 2020 ✨<br /><br />These books have been so formative to me as a reader, writer, and person for so many years, and it’s surreal to realize that the series ends in just a month and a few days. I’ve grown up hand in hand with these characters— I’ve navigated new school hallways with my paperback carefully tucked in my bag, made my first internet friends in forums on the author’s website, and traveled to my first book conventions in New York City and Charleston because of these stories. Over the years, I’ve recognized so many facets of myself in Sophie, Agatha, and Tedros, and I’ve found my own insecurities and conflicts mirrored in their relationships with one another. I’ve taken solace in their beauty and imperfections, appreciating the validation that their complexity brought to me during those scary and magical moments that define growing up. <br /><br />Now, as I graduate high school and prepare to begin college in the fall, it only makes sense that my childhood friends also graduate school and prepare to face the woods ahead of them, but that doesn’t make this release date all feel any less strange. I’m going to miss these kids. &lt;3<br /><br />✨June 3rd, 2020✨<br /><br />I finished the book at 1:30 am last night, and oh my god, I sobbed! I genuinely could not have dreamed of a better concussion to this series, and I feel so grateful to have gotten such a good ending to a story that I love this dearly and matters this much to me. The book was beautiful, bittersweet, satisfying, and so, so rewarding.<br /><br />It’s been a heavy and challenging year for everyone -- I mean, I was supposed to have my graduation ceremony last night. I've admittedly been struggling to get myself moving forward again in the absence of normal rituals, but I think this book was what I needed to feel ready for whatever comes next. Closing the back cover of One True King felt an awful lot like closing this chapter of my life, like some sense of closure. <br /><br />I really do owe so much to this story.<br /><br />✨June 8th, 2020✨<br /><br />Okay, initial heart ache and nostalgia aside, there's so much gold in this book to dig up and appreciate, and I think I'm finally in the right headspace to do so! Yay! I might even take a highlighter and pen to my unsigned edition for annotating in a week or two... just no one tell my 13-year-old self, who I can already hear shrieking in the back of my mind "bOOK CRIME!"<br /><br /><b>SPOILERS AHEAD. CONSIDER YOURSELF WARNED. &lt;3</b><br /><br />One True King definitely abides by its infamous SGE branding and supplies many wild twists and turns. Even the few events and deaths that I knew absolutely had to happen were written in such a creative and backwards way that when they did unfold, I still found myself surprised. To name one in particular...<br /><br /><b>M E R L I N</b><br /><br />It's no surprise that Merlin is a favorite of mine (you can find me on Instagram as @merlins_celestium), but still, I knew he couldn't survive the ending. That's just the way of middle grade and young adult literature: the main character(s) lose their mentors before or during the final battle. We've seen this happen numerous times before in SGE with Professor Sader, Lady Lesso, Callis, and Professor Dovey, and Agatha even makes a point of it while sitting with Guinevere (who also meets a tragic end, yikes) in One True King by remarking on how cruel her fairytale is to the grown-ups.<br /><br />And yet, Soman didn't kill off Merlin in the first few chapters, like I had expected him to. Instead, he limited Merlin's ability to aid the protagonists in their tests with the aging spell, which allowed him to keep the wizard alive until <i>literally the last line of the book</i>. Not only was this trick smart and admirable, but aging Merlin backwards was one of my favorite parts of the story. It was immensely amusing to watch Agatha and Tedros try to parent (their old teacher, nonetheless), and Merlin's commentary as he grew older added so much to scenes and dialogue. It also made me realize what a terrific mother Agatha would make, which was so lovely to see <i>without</i> any sort of cheesy or overdone flash-forwarded epilogue. <br /><br />This all goes to say that when Merlin eventually did die at the end, I actually found myself surprised! Even though this was the one thing I went into the book expecting would happen, I got so caught up in the story and Merlin's hilarious adventures as a teenager that I completely forgot that his time as an old man was dwindling and that couldn’t, in fact, survive the book. And I don't know if anyone else had this experience, but his death reminded me an awful lot of the end of Les Mis? Whatever truly did me in, I ugly cried for those last two pages. "The work is done?" Damn. <br /><br /><b>T E D R O S</b><br /><br />For me, the more I love something, the harder I find it to explain why. So, this section will be short. <br /><br />Tedros definitely wasn't my favorite character at the start of the series, but the Camelot Years really fleshed him out and showed us a side to him that had me 100% falling in love. These three books became his coming-of-age saga, and he's grown so much from the insecure and foolish little boy that we first met back in book one -- it warms my heart so much. I am <i>fiercely</i> proud of everything that this boy has accomplished over the course of all six books, and goddamnit, he deserves that crown. Camelot is lucky to have him as a leader. (He even pulled a f*ucking Jesus in the end! Holy cow! He did that! ) <br /><br />I wish I could give him a hug. :’)<br /><br /><b>R E L A T I O N S H I P S</b> <br /><br />Speaking of Tedros, the Tagatha in this novel was TOP NOTCH. These kids have been endgame since book one, but the last few installments to the series really put their relationship through the wringer. All of the bickering and miscommunication has Not been cute. I’m so happy that this book focused so much on them developing trust in their relationship, which was so sorely needed, and I was impressed by how well they grew together as a partnership. I finally feel confident that they're fit to rule a kingdom. They’ve learned a lot, and it’s so nice to see them happy. Merlin put it perfectly: they really are such wondrous souls. I think they'll make great rulers, and maybe parents, too.<br /><br />(That was a joke. Please. They can wait. They're, like, 17 or something. Please let them wait.)<br /><br />Not to mention, we finally got Hophie! I know that this pairing is somewhat controversial among readers, but I've been waiting on their ship to sail for years, so don't you DARE ruin this moment for me. This is the ending that Sophie deserved, that Hort deserved, and that we all deserved. You can’t convince me otherwise. I'm also still <i>so</i> fragile from Hort's near-death experience, so just, don't talk to me for a while. Thank you.<br /><br />And FINALLY. THE MOMENT THAT WE’VE ALL BEEN WAITING FOR. Hester and Anadil. That's it. That's the review. I've been dying for confirmation on their relationship ever since all of their ridiculous flirting in the Ever Never Handbook, and I'm thrilled that we finally got it carved in as canon. Their banter in this book was amazing, incredible, show-stopping, marvelous, and had me swooning and giggling on every other page. All the "Ew, like an Ever Boy?" comments killed me, and all I have to say is that I better be invited to the wedding. <br /><br /><b>S U R P R I S E S</b> <br /><br />Rafal being revealed as Japeth and Rhian's father hit me like a ton of bricks. Not only was I a) unabashedly shocked and b) horrified for poor Sophie, but also c) I felt absolutely awful for Rhian, who was lied to his entire life. I wish we could have resurrected <i>him</i>, Jesus Christ (pun intended). He really deserved better.<br /><br />Speaking of characters who deserved better, once the Queen referred to her daughter as Betty, I immediately made the connection to Bettina, and I had a sinking suspicion that things couldn't end well for her. We needed her Mother on our side, and Japeth murdering her daughter was quite effective in doing that. That said, I really wish we had gotten more of her character! She was really only alive for 20 pages before, but I still managed to absolutely fall in love with her. So. Who wants to start a Bettina and Rhian Deserved Better Campaign with me? We meet tomorrow at dawn.<br /><br />I also did NOT expect Chaddick to be the eldest son of King Arthur. Yes, it makes perfect sense in hindsight, and I feel like an absolute fool for not realizing it earlier, but oh my god.<br /><br /><b>C L O S U R E</b><br /><br />Overall, the vibes in this book? Were immaculate. I haven't felt as blissfully immersed in a story as I did while reading this one for maybe years. The writing is just that phenomenal. When I read the last half for the first time on Tuesday night, the events felt so real, it was as if I were actually in the story. I completely forgot I was reading. I don't know when I’ll get to feel that way about a book next, as it’s been so long, but it was amazing while it lasted. These books are actual magic.<br /><br />I was also pleasantly surprised by how many loose ends were tied up, considering the scope of this series. The few things that were left unanswered felt purposeful and right, and the ending felt perfect. I liked that it still left a dash of mystery in its wake, since what the book chose to focus on and end felt more powerful. <br /><br />This isn’t even to mention all the small moments throughout the book that made me pause to smile or cry. Hester responding to Dot's discovery about being Half-Ever with "Nobody's perfect" made me melt. Merlin's flashback to his last time with Tedros in the Ender Forest made me sob. Sophie picking up the piece of cake was so simple, yet so heartfelt! I find it funny that it’s these quiet moments that define as epic of a series as the School for Good and Evil for me, but it’s true -- they really do. These books make the most ambitious and grand fairytales feel magically intimate and personal for its readers. I’m sure Agatha and Sophie would be proud.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12570770829585081275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3029877760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3029877760" />
    <a title="Garg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42804085-garg"><img alt="Garg" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3029877760?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Garg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Garg" href="/user/show/42804085-garg">Garg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42804085-garg?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3029877760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17607495313218874039">PreRead:<br/><br/>My hopes and dreams for this book (CAUTION: THIS CONTAINS SPOILERS FOR PREVIOUS BOOKS IN THE SERIES)<br/><br/>1: Sophie finds happiness (probably through love though not with Hort cause they don’t seem like a good couple)<br/>2: Hort find love and gets over Sophie (he can’t commit to Nicola because of Sophie) <br/>3: Agatha dumps Tedros (or their relationship matures it just needs some work before I can really ship it)<br/>4: Agatha gives Sophie the love that Sophie deserves (not only the sisterly love but the l</span>
  <span id="freeText17607495313218874039" style="display:none">PreRead:<br /><br />My hopes and dreams for this book (CAUTION: THIS CONTAINS SPOILERS FOR PREVIOUS BOOKS IN THE SERIES)<br /><br />1: Sophie finds happiness (probably through love though not with Hort cause they don’t seem like a good couple)<br />2: Hort find love and gets over Sophie (he can’t commit to Nicola because of Sophie) <br />3: Agatha dumps Tedros (or their relationship matures it just needs some work before I can really ship it)<br />4: Agatha gives Sophie the love that Sophie deserves (not only the sisterly love but the love of best friends neither of which she has ever given Sophie enough of) <br />5: Kiko, Beatrix, Anadil, and Dot find love (not necessarily with each other but I think Beatrix and Anadil could work. Maybe?)<br />6: Rafal comes back to be Sophie’s true love, also character development... but mainly for her (this is more an idea of a possible thing than a real hope, it just seems like an intriguing idea)<br />7-infinity: See number one <br /><br />I do hope for more character based things because he always throws me for a loop, so I’m too nervous to even try to guess what will happen plot wise. In reality, all of these things might not happen and I can still be happy with the book... as long as Sophie gets what she deserves. GO SOPHIE! And Agatha really needs to dump Tedros and Tedros needs to hand over his kingdom to a better king (Agatha, Sophie, a parliament, or other... almost anyone but him unless he and the relationship matures). <br /><br />Title:<br /><br />The one true king. I mean, it’s probably Tedros especially with the ending of the last book and the last ring. But... he’s not really worthy yet? So idk. <br /><br />Cover:<br /><br />I don’t like it (though the swan crowns are cool). Sophie and Agatha’s hair is so weird and shiny instead of the flatter and more cartooned look of the others. And is it just me or is their skin green? And even if this is an attempt to make them look “older”, A Crystal of Time had the characters around the same age, and they looked the same as the other covers. <br />It wouldn’t be that bad if it wasn’t so inconsistent with the styles of the other book covers. Where did my precious girls go? <br />Honestly though, Sophie and Agatha just look WEIRD on the cover. I respect if you like it, but I just don’t. Maybe I could like it if it wasn’t so different from the others. I just think that the girls should look like the same people across all of the covers<br /><br />After reading (with spoilers)<br /><br />I did not see any of that coming. Hort and Sophie were actually cute together, they both grew a lot. Similarly with Tedros and Agatha, their relationship really blossomed. Still not a fan if the cover, but I really liked the book. I didn’t see Chaddick coming or Uma’s importance and I define my didn’t see merlin’s huge importance and death. My favorite scene is probably the one where Agatha and Sophie get to be king. A question I have: who’s the new school master?<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_3382459143" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3382459143" />
    <a title="Eli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55468947-eli"><img alt="Eli" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3382459143?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eli" href="/user/show/55468947-eli">Eli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3382459143&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3382459143" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13761935974938555628">Man, to be honest, I expected so much more from this magical series. It had so many twists and turns that kept me hooked, compelling characters that broke the usual stereotypes presented in fairytales, and intricate worldbuilding that really made the book pop out. <br/><br/>But there's a lot of potential that was wasted on this book, which I really wanted to enjoy since it's the last installment of a series that I'm absolutely obsessed with.<br/><br/><br/>WARNING: MAJOR SPOILERS AHEAD!!!<br/><br/><br/><br/>PLOT:<br/><br/>The pacing of 3/4 of the sto</span>
  <span id="freeText13761935974938555628" style="display:none">Man, to be honest, I expected so much more from this magical series. It had so many twists and turns that kept me hooked, compelling characters that broke the usual stereotypes presented in fairytales, and intricate worldbuilding that really made the book pop out. <br /><br />But there's a lot of potential that was wasted on this book, which I really wanted to enjoy since it's the last installment of a series that I'm absolutely obsessed with.<br /><br /><br />WARNING: MAJOR SPOILERS AHEAD!!!<br /><br /><br /><br />PLOT:<br /><br />The pacing of 3/4 of the story was pretty okay for me. The challenges were really exciting, with the unexpected twists in the trials such as how Agatha swallowed the pearl instead of the two boys, the encounter between Tedeos and the genie, the 4 Agathas scene, and more. There's also a lot of girl power throughout it (like how the girls were chosen as the knights of Jaunt Jolie, how Reena handled herself as the princess, etc.)<br /><br />I LOVED Tagatha in this one too, (of course it's my favorite ship and Agatha's also my favorite character), since they developed more maturity throughout their journey with Agatha learning how to trust Tedros and Tedros becoming less cocky, realizing his flaws and facing his insecurities head-on. Baby Merlin was really cute and funny too! His parts cracked me up. Sophie and Hort's ship was a really good one as well, with Sophie learning how to open her heart more and Hort always being there for her even if she didn't realize how much he cared for her. Though I hated how there were so many deaths in the book. I really wanted to sympathize with their deaths, I really do, but the emotions were kind off knocked out of me because there were too many deaths too count. The only one that really hit me was perhaps Guinevere's. Betty's death felt so rushed, since she was just introduced early on in the book and got killed just a few chapters later. <br /><br />What really disappointed me was the end part. <br /><br />I hated how Hort "died" that easily from saving Sophie from the carriage because come on, after all those "I love Sophie, she's my soulmate, blablabla," and how Sophie realizes that her heart is opening up to Hort, I really think he should've had a better "death" scene. Sure I teared up a bit, but it didn't really work out for me entirely. Especially with their ship going on ever since Book 1.<br /><br />The last trial was really underwhelming for me. That last-minute twist of young Tedros wishing to be revived from death didn't resonate with me, since it seemed shoved between the plot just to give Tedros a reason to live. I expected the last challenge to really prove that Tedros was a deserving king, not just through his long speech but more through his actions. Maybe deep inside I wanted a bigger fight or challenge, one that didn't just expose Japeth, pull out the sword and just kill him. Plus we didn't even fully know what happened to Japeth after that, how Tedros reclaimed the other kingdoms' trust again, and the overall aftermath. We just skipped to Tedros and Agatha's wedding, with that abrupt revelation that Hort was still alive, and then Merlin's death as well. All of this felt very rushed, and it saddened me since I wanted to read about how Sophie realizes what made her happy all along (like an ending that emulated the same feeling as Book 3, even if she did end up with Hort or not), and Agatha walking down the aisle with a wedding that would really radiate the spirit of her and Tedros' love and everything they went through. I wanted it to seal their wonderful story and to see all the other characters like the coven, the teachers, and the other fourth years, all come together for an epic ending. I'm disappointed to see the story I really invested in becoming rushed and feeling incomplete.<br /><br />But the School for Good and Evil has gripped me for so many years, and the characters will have a special place in my heart always. Just wished that we could've gotten a better farewell to such a good series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13761935974938555628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3425137986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Sara Saif" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33555642-sara-saif"><img alt="Sara Saif" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567114974p2/33555642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3425137986?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Saif" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Saif" href="/user/show/33555642-sara-saif">Sara Saif</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=you-re-cute-but-not-that-cute">you-re-cute-but-not-that-cute</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3425137986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4837219393513159563"><p>The End of Ends...Right up until a third trilogy comes out, amirite?</p><br/>What a hopelessly convoluted story! I couldn't keep anything straight. I've always had trouble pinpointing what exactly I find off about these books. They're absurd and funny on many levels, each getting progressively less so with each book. But, it just never loses the silliness I guess. It used to be amusing, with the last three books it was just confusing. <br/><p>The plot is all over the place. The many tracks and diversions and sub</p></span>
  <span id="freeText4837219393513159563" style="display:none"><p>The End of Ends...Right up until a third trilogy comes out, amirite?</p><br>What a hopelessly convoluted story! I couldn't keep anything straight. I've always had trouble pinpointing what exactly I find off about these books. They're absurd and funny on many levels, each getting progressively less so with each book. But, it just never loses the silliness I guess. It used to be amusing, with the last three books it was just confusing. <br><p>The plot is all over the place. The many tracks and diversions and subplots at once complicated and crazy. A small example of this I can come up with right now is the Cave of Wishes part. Specifically, the genie telling who his true love was, and that too to the same person's beloved. What in the name of bananas was <i>that</i>? It was so obviously randomly cooked up and it made no sense.</p><br>There are numerous small things similarly random and nonsensical in this trilogy, and the last book is just when my patience ran out.<br><p>The back and forth in this series is an astounding level of stupid. You think things have progressed, people have developed, but they revert back to how they were before in the next instant and on and on it goes. Hort and Sophie, for example. What I wished for happened but it happened like this:</p><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594016534ra/29768727.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And so did everything else. Tedros's journey to becoming the One True King was tedious and infuriating to say the least. I thought I wanted this series but I thought wrong. The End.<br></span>

<div id="review_3383702876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3383702876" />
    <a title="G Daniels" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114800055-g-daniels"><img alt="G Daniels" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598751990p2/114800055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3383702876?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="G Daniels" class="user" itemprop="url" name="G Daniels" href="/user/show/114800055-g-daniels">G Daniels</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062695215" href="/book/show/50175196-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3383702876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10461986218431611420">Overall I enjoyed the series as a bit of light fluff. I must confess that somehow I missed #5 in the series skipping right from book #4 to 6, but don't think I really missed too much that I couldn't pick up on the story., Though I am sure there is a lot explained in book #5 that would have answered some of the questions I had when I begun #6, it's not so importanat to me to learn what I missed to go back and read it now. The series wasn't THAT good in my opinion.<br/>Of course from the beginning, you</span>
  <span id="freeText10461986218431611420" style="display:none">Overall I enjoyed the series as a bit of light fluff. I must confess that somehow I missed #5 in the series skipping right from book #4 to 6, but don't think I really missed too much that I couldn't pick up on the story., Though I am sure there is a lot explained in book #5 that would have answered some of the questions I had when I begun #6, it's not so importanat to me to learn what I missed to go back and read it now. The series wasn't THAT good in my opinion.<br />Of course from the beginning, you could pretty well predict the ending, after all it WAS supposed to be a fairy tale complete w/ the "happily ever after". So if you were looking for any major diversions or some dark twist at the end, you will be sadly disappointed. If you are desirous of some light entertainment that does not engage your mind very much, where everything turns out to be butterflies, (blue ones of course) and unicorns, (sans unicorns, no unicorns in this series, sorry), you are in the right place. This is a nice escape and I believe is geared more for middle school age children, but can be enjoyed by any age who just wants some light entertainment and a simple diversion. If you are looking for some deep hidden wisdom in these pages you will be sorely disappointed, this is not a series for you. But if you want an entertaining escape, I would recommend it. <br />Now for the parts that I found wanting. To begin w/: Tedros. He was a whiney little arrogant weenie throughout. Agatha was way too good for him, and actually so was Sophie for that matter. They should have kicked him to the curb and Sophie and Agatha could have had their "happily ever after" together without his whiney arse. Some will of course disagree w/ me on this which is okay, you have a right to your opinion. To me Tedros was just an insecure jerk and when he finally got an epiphany, it was a bit contrived. This whole entire series showed Agatha to be the true hero and Sophie was her devoted sidekick. Tedros was just an anchor weighing down Agatha and preventing her from achieving her full potential. <br />Another thing that I found difficult and it may only be due to my weak mind, but I had difficulty with keeping all the characters straight. Characters would float in and out and I could not remember if they were an Evil or a Good or a Never or an Ever, or who they were related to. It got very complicated. A list of characters at the beginning or the end of the book would have been a very helpful resource. If you are just beginning this series, I may suggest taking notes as to who the characters you are introduced to so you can keep them straight. Hint, Sophie and Agatha are the main characters throughout. :)<br />What I liked: I really enjoyed Agatha and Sophie's relationship. Also how they both grew and became more than what they originally believed. Agatha was quite clever, strategizing, relying on her wits, she was very independent, strong and self-reliant, (qualities Tedros was lacking and could use). Sophie, you just have to love her. She appears so shallow but underneath there are some very deep and strong currents. She is a lot more complicated than what is originally perceived and shows strengths all her own. Their friendship and reliance on each other was a testament and showed a strong loyalty. Speaking of loyalty they did get a lot of support from their friends, even when it was extremely dangerous and not necessarily in the best interests of themselves. I also really enjoyed the three witches. The one w/ the "chocolate touch" was a bit over the top and would have been better served w/ a different power, but overall they were a lot of fun throughout the series. <br />So in conclusion it was an enjoyable read, but not sure I would care to revisit the School, nor see how Agatha and Sophie ended up beyond the end of the 6th book. It was afun ride but now that it is over, I don't care to ride it again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10461986218431611420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3078541879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3078541879" />
    <a title="Katja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92441514-katja"><img alt="Katja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548014815p2/92441514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3078541879?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katja" href="/user/show/92441514-katja">Katja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3078541879&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3078541879" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3341129625031204505">My mind is still spinning! What an amazing world, an amazing adventure! Since book 1, I've always been pulled in from the very first page. And the plot twists! Just when I think I got it or there can't be anymore-Surprise!! My heart aches with Tedros and Agatha as they learn the real truth about Arthur's other son. And the soul ripping character deaths! I should be used to it and expect it with this series, but somehow I just couldn't. What I really love about this book and the series is the cha</span>
  <span id="freeText3341129625031204505" style="display:none">My mind is still spinning! What an amazing world, an amazing adventure! Since book 1, I've always been pulled in from the very first page. And the plot twists! Just when I think I got it or there can't be anymore-Surprise!! My heart aches with Tedros and Agatha as they learn the real truth about Arthur's other son. And the soul ripping character deaths! I should be used to it and expect it with this series, but somehow I just couldn't. What I really love about this book and the series is the character growth of Tedros ♥️ Agatha; plus, Sofie. But especially Tedros who I realized in book 2 was really a tragic character damaged by those who were supposed to love him. I enjoyed watching his transformation from an immature distrustful scared boy into a self confident, good man and a good king worthy of Agatha.<br /><br />It's with regret I can only give 4 stars due to the very last chapter (at the very end of it), which focuses on Merlin. This entire series is the story of Agatha and Sofie, Agatha and Tedros and Sofie and Hort. Although beloved by all and one of my favorite characters, this is not Merlin's story. I loved the touching final scene of them surrounding a dying Merlin, "The work is done," however, the series should NOT stop on Merlin. Literally! The story came to an immediate "stop" instead of an "end," which is something all authors must avoid. In the final moment, the story did not feel over because it was missing a chapter. One more chapter, even a short one, should have been written with a saddened, but determined Agatha and Tedros going forth with their wedding. They say "I do," and seal their love with a kiss in front of their friends, which officially declares their Happily Ever After. Since this is...you know...a fairy tale.<br /><br />I'm so happy Sofie found her prince even if he wasn't what she was expecting. And honestly? Me neither! I remember first meeting Hort and thinking like Sofie, Eewww! NO WAY!! GROSS!! Then Book 3 happened, but I wasn't sure if Hort and Sofie would or could make it. Yet, they did make it! After everything they've been through they matured and are finally together and it's beautiful. Too bad Chainani didn't write one more chapter of the actual Tedros and Agatha wedding because then all the Sofie/Hort fans like myself could've had another chance to see them holding each other. Just as the wish fish showed Hort back in Book 3.😉</span>

I genuinely enjoyed delving back into the fairy tale of Agatha and Sophie, however what kept me from devouring this book at breakneck pace was the often confused perspective. The author writes in third person close, but frequently switches character perspective without notice, causing many of the book’s climaxes to read confusedly. Merely a personal reasoning behind my four star review. I still highly recommend this conclusion to a wonderful </span>
  <span id="freeText16629946194042328422" style="display:none">I teetered between four and five stars with this one. The author writes in third person close, but frequently switches character perspective without notice, causing many of the book’s climaxes to read confusedly. <div id="review_3371168735" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3371168735" />
    <a title="Isolt Sayre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112735242-isolt-sayre"><img alt="Isolt Sayre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605549526p2/112735242.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isolt Sayre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isolt Sayre" href="/user/show/112735242-isolt-sayre">Isolt Sayre</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3371168735" class="readable"
