<span id="freeTextContainer356937555660344122">I will start off by saying I got up at FIVE IN THE MORNING for this book, as it came out today. Wow.....<br/>SPOILERS BELOW! YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED!<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>I can’t say for sure if the writing for this book is as good as the others, because I tore through it, ready to reach the “End of Ends.” But the storytelling was SUPERB. I was on the edge of my seat (okay, bed) with anticipation the entire time. The idea is that King Arthur had an idea there would be two people vying for the crown, and so he set up 3 tests </span>
  <span id="freeText356937555660344122" style="display:none">I will start off by saying I got up at FIVE IN THE MORNING for this book, as it came out today. Wow.....<br />SPOILERS BELOW! YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />I can’t say for sure if the writing for this book is as good as the others, because I tore through it, ready to reach the “End of Ends.” But the storytelling was SUPERB. I was on the edge of my seat (okay, bed) with anticipation the entire time. The idea is that King Arthur had an idea there would be two people vying for the crown, and so he set up 3 tests to pick a winner. The first test goes normally... except like everyone dies. Kei, and Robin Hood meets their end, William nearly gets pecked to death and WAIT! He’s Tristan’s younger brother! (And he’s gay, poor Kiko) Then Agatha, who is SO in love with Tedros, accidentally swallows a magic pearl, and so, for the next test, either Japeth or Tedros have to kill Agatha. And I’m sobbing because Agatha is SO GOOD and deserves a HAPPY ENDING and Tedros might have to KILL HER! So, then, a bunch of magic stuff happens. Uma meets Kaveen, her former husband, a bunch of ladies (Kiko, Beatrix, etc.) band together with the Queen of Jaunt Jolie to form a little band of soldiers to save the world while Guinevere and Tedros make wished in Aladdin’s cave. We find out that Japeth loved Aric, then GUINEVERE DIES! Also, Maid Marian is Dot’s MOTHER! Guinevere’s death replaces Agatha’s, so Agatha is alive!!!! And Hort rescues Sophie after breaking up with Nic, gets severely wounded, and proclaims his love for her. Sophie goes into emotional shock, because her one true love is dead, and I’m crying because WHY???? They were SO CUTE together. Then there’a bunch of Excaliburs that pop up in all the kingdoms, and we find out that<br />1. Japeth is the son of Evelyn Sader<br />2. His father is the Green Knight, a.k.a. Sir Kay, a.k.a. Japeth <br />3. Just kidding, he’s not<br />4. JAPETH’S FATHER IS THE SCHOOL MASTER A.K.A. RAFAL WHAT IS THIS WHY ALSO EWWWWW SOPHIE YOU DATED RHIAN AND HIS DAD<br />5. That’s the craziest thing that happened. Moving on...<br />6. Just kidding. It gets crazier<br />7. CHADDICK IS THE SON OF GRISELLA GREMLAINE AND KING ARTHUR, CONCEIVED THE NIGHT BEFORE ARTHUR’S WEDDING<br />8. CHADDICK IS WAS THE EDLEST SON OF KING ARTHUR<br />9. CHADDICK’S DEAD<br />10. WHAT. ON. EARTH. JUST. HAPPENED. (I’m suing Soman Chainani, because I almost had a heart attack caused by surprise)<br />So, yeah, Chaddick’s blood can fool Excalibur, so that’s how Rhian and Rafal Japeth(!) were able to pull Excalibur. Rafal Japeth snuck a piece of cloth with Chaddick’s blood on it on Rhian, so Rhian pulled Excalibur, STILL THINKING HE WAS ARTHUR’S SON.<br />Then Rafal Japeth cheats and uses Chaddick’s blood to pull Excalibur, which was in Chaddick’s house, and LOPS OFF TEDROS’S HEAD.<br />WHY?????.<br />I’M CRYING TOO, AGATHA!<br />NOT FAIR.<br />JUST KIDDING!<br />He got an magic apple from the Lady of the Lake! His head pops back on! He exposes Rafal Japeth as a fraud!<br />YES!<br />Japeth loses his head.<br />Good Riddance!<br />Then, it’s wedding day for Agatha and Tedros, and Sophie’s rather depressed, because Hort’s dead.<br />JUST KIDDING! HORT’S ALIVE! HE WAS RESCUED BY YUBA THE GNOME! THEN, SOPHIE AND HORT KISS!<br />It was epic. Period.<br />Then Merlin dies, and it’s over. The series is done. <br /><br /><br /><br />This book was great based on storytelling. I’ll reread it and see if I can enjoy the writing more. <br />Baby Merlin is the best thing EVER.<br />The character development is good with the main characters. I actually felt sorry for Rafal Japeth at one point.<br />The Coven rocks. (I never realized how much I shipped Hester and Anadil until I did)<br />I have two complaints.<br />1. This book is LONG, and even then, it’s sometimes rushed at scenes.<br />2. There was not enough Nicola, Beatrix, Kiko, Willam, or Bogden. So sad, but there was so much going on already.<br /><br /><br />This is a great concluding book. Emotional roller coaster, however. BEWARE!</span>

    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12062907-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576461714p2/12062907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2947936093?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2947936093" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12858281137595022412">Very bittersweet to say goodbye to this series. I’m so torn on this final book. The ending was technically what I wanted (my big ships happened), and there were some really fantastic scenes, but I think a lot of character development was pushed aside to make room for an excessively complicated plot. In some ways, I think that was true for the Camelot years as a whole. The first trilogy did such a fantastic job balancing character growth with high stakes and intricate plot, but this trilogy felt </span>
  <span id="freeText12858281137595022412" style="display:none">Very bittersweet to say goodbye to this series. I’m so torn on this final book. The ending was technically what I wanted (my big ships happened), and there were some really fantastic scenes, but I think a lot of character development was pushed aside to make room for an excessively complicated plot. In some ways, I think that was true for the Camelot years as a whole. The first trilogy did such a fantastic job balancing character growth with high stakes and intricate plot, but this trilogy felt very heavy on setting up the plot (by the time they found the big answers they were looking for, I still felt like I was waiting for someone to say “Wait, Nope, that’s not it” because that happened so often). Especially towards the end, it seemed the big internal struggles the characters were facing were “fixed” kind of suddenly. <br /><br />I still love this series (horrible, horrible fatphobia throughout aside), but the conclusion left me wishing for another book or two of just the characters growing and learning without secrets upon secrets and twists upon twists. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12858281137595022412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3025095268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2166530334699779391"><i>“Because life was fleeting and pointless unless you let yourself enjoy it, savor it, down to its lightest, most insignificant moments.”</i><br/><br/>This book was definitely not one of the light insignificant moments, it was the end of a series that was a large expanse of wonder for me as a reader. It honestly brought so much light into my life and upon finishing it I feel a little lost inside. I fell in love with EVERY character in the first book and to watch Chainani kill them off one by one or help them gr</span>
  <span id="freeText2166530334699779391" style="display:none"><i>“Because life was fleeting and pointless unless you let yourself enjoy it, savor it, down to its lightest, most insignificant moments.”</i><br /><br />This book was definitely not one of the light insignificant moments, it was the end of a series that was a large expanse of wonder for me as a reader. It honestly brought so much light into my life and upon finishing it I feel a little lost inside. I fell in love with EVERY character in the first book and to watch Chainani kill them off one by one or help them grow 🥺 my heart y’all my HEART 💔<br /><br />What I love most about this book is everything it is not. This is love and life in its purest forms, as a YA fantasy reader I read a lot of books where the love interests describe the fire of lust they have when they see each other and I read them and like them but none of them had this childlike yet honest view of life. What Tedros and Agatha have I have NEVER read in a book before. It was not something rooted in lust it was a love that you learn from and love that you grow into and a love that was pure. Long story short there was absolutely no steamy scenes in this whole series, and me a romance addict was ok with that? THAT tells you the MASTERY of his writing. <br /><br />^^*i was looking for the word clean read 🥴*<br />**do NOT get me wrong there was enough romance in this series to make any girl, guy or anyone of any persuasion swoon and melt**<br /><br /><i>“This is about letting yourself take chances at love and not giving up. That’s why love is the ultimate test. It forces us to grow, to be better, and even then, sometimes it’s not enough. We get in our own way. We’re our own worst villains. But only a true villain believes he can control love. Love can’t be controlled any more than a wildfire can. It lives in the balance of fate and free will, Man and Pen. We do our part, we hope, we wish . . . but it writes its own story in its own time, the way it’s meant to be.” </i><br /><br />Do not misunderstand me this books contemplates evil, as well the goodness in evil, the evil in good and maybe even the grey between. You watch characters grow realistically from thirteen year olds to young adults and it’s painful, as life is, you lose people, you gain friends then lose them too, but the lessons and the love? It’s permanent it’s real, and it worth it. <br /><br />An amazing end to one of my all time favourite series and I’m am still torn whether I should cry normally or cry really hard? I cannot wait for the movie because YES this will be a movie!!!! And I cannot wait to see the characters I love on the screen, I will be the movies biggest fan until it comes out but until then I have some crying to do 😔<br /><br />Excerpts From<br />The School for Good and Evil #6: One True King<br />Soman Chainani<br />This material may be protected by copyright</span>

<div id="review_3489595592" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3489595592" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83936113-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604329920p2/83936113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3489595592?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/83936113-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3489595592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer973933127957803555">i was going to write a very long review about this but have kind of run out of energy, so i'll do my best.<br/><br/>so, <i>the school for good and evil</i> was my favourite series when i was 11, and obviously since being 11 my reading tastes have changed a LOT (as you would expect 😂). i think i have also become a lot more critical in my opinions of books, and that means as i have got older and i have continued with this series, i have noticed some things that i didn't like too much.<br/><br/>i just felt, that in a lot of </span>
  <span id="freeText973933127957803555" style="display:none">i was going to write a very long review about this but have kind of run out of energy, so i'll do my best.<br /><br />so, <i>the school for good and evil</i> was my favourite series when i was 11, and obviously since being 11 my reading tastes have changed a LOT (as you would expect 😂). i think i have also become a lot more critical in my opinions of books, and that means as i have got older and i have continued with this series, i have noticed some things that i didn't like too much.<br /><br />i just felt, that in a lot of places, the author included quite a few lines and ideas that seemed to perpetuate toxic masculinity and possessiveness within relationships. for example: '"may i ask why you couldn't keep your wife?" said the knight.' this statement gives the impression that a person's wife is their possession, and this way of objectifying women is never addressed in the book. this sort of thing happens in quite a few other places, and it's never stated in the book that objectifying women is wrong. since the author included so much of this, i would have expected that somewhere in the book it's mentioned how wrong this is?<br /><br />tedros (hah my autocorrect just tried to change this to testosterone,,, fitting) and agatha are constantly possessive of each other throughout the book and in their chapters the other is always referred to as 'his princess' or 'her prince'. this would be fine if it only happened once or twice, but this possessive language is used every few sentences, which suggests to me that the characters view their partners more as belongings than equals.<br /><br />there is also the constant reinforcement of gender roles throughout the book, as the test is always viewed as only tedros', and when agatha gets involved he gets angry at her, and almost suggests that he would be happier if agatha just assumed the role of a stereotypical princess: just to sit around and look pretty. i also just get sexist and misogynist vibes from tedros, but who's surprised 🙄? <br /><br />however, on a slightly more positive note, i feel that soman chainani did try to be slightly more inclusive, which is good (there were a few LGBTQ+ relationships eluded to, but the rep still could have been better).<br /><br />just a quick note on the plot, since i don't think i've really discussed that yet - i thought it was pretty slow at the beginning, but did pick up a bit towards the end and i enjoyed the conclusion!</span>
  <a data-text-id="973933127957803555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3439262069" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3439262069" />
    <a title="Shawne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/284285-shawne"><img alt="Shawne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187283272p2/284285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3439262069?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawne" href="/user/show/284285-shawne">Shawne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/284285-shawne?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3439262069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3068499983635649826">I'm a completist so have now made it through all six books in Soman Chainani's fantasy fairy-tale series. I... guess I'm glad I read this book just so I can see how it all ends, but boy. It was rough to get through this (supposedly) final installment.<br/><br/>Chainani's belaboured plotting is on full display here - the backstory twisting in and out of itself with such abandon that you'll find yourself quite puzzled by the number of times the narrative rewrites itself to fit the capricious demands of its </span>
  <span id="freeText3068499983635649826" style="display:none">I'm a completist so have now made it through all six books in Soman Chainani's fantasy fairy-tale series. I... guess I'm glad I read this book just so I can see how it all ends, but boy. It was rough to get through this (supposedly) final installment.<br /><br />Chainani's belaboured plotting is on full display here - the backstory twisting in and out of itself with such abandon that you'll find yourself quite puzzled by the number of times the narrative rewrites itself to fit the capricious demands of its author. (Some might find this brilliantly meta in a book all about a magic Pen controlling the fates of the characters it writes about, but I found it more annoying than not.)<br /><br />The final act of the book, in particular, occasionally feels like Chainani just writing whatever the heck he wants whenever he wants (see: the Sugar Queen), even as his basic plot keeps unravelling to reveal more twists that barely make sense. Arthur's romantic tribulations are truly a sight to behold (Guinevere and Gremlaine and Sader, oh my!), and feel almost nonsensical in the way they unfold - Chainani simply creating wrinkles that weren't there before to fit the purposes of his heavily re-engineered plot as he excruciatingly expands his series into a second trilogy.<br /><br />That's not to say there weren't things to enjoy. There were some really good moments and insights - I liked how this book handled Merlin as a character; his final appearance in it actually elicited a genuine emotional response from me. Some of the many MANY twists were good - chiefly to do with Tedros' growth and maturity - which allow him to become the King he was not equipped to be at the start of the series.<br /><br />In these moments, Chainani succeeds almost in spite of himself, his bloated plotting sometimes giving way to moments of quite lovely clarity and insight for his characters and their relationships with one another.<br /><br />Last, but certainly not least - Chainani sorely needed an editor to hurry things along, and also to shape everything into something more coherent. Still can't get used to his unusual verb usage, even after six increasingly long books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3068499983635649826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3377131374&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3377131374" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12514335392631161215">I was a little sad and disappointed quite honestly. At the beginning of the series, Agatha was a strong independent character, but as we reached book 6 she turned into less of a leader for Tedros to shine(Ironically made his character more bearable). I also really hated how we got less Sophie chapters and that basically, Agatha didn’t want her to live in Camelot with them, and to make Agatha look like less of a dick Soman our dear author decides to randomly bring Hort back to Sophie... now don't</span>
  <span id="freeText12514335392631161215" style="display:none">I was a little sad and disappointed quite honestly. At the beginning of the series, Agatha was a strong independent character, but as we reached book 6 she turned into less of a leader for Tedros to shine(Ironically made his character more bearable). I also really hated how we got less Sophie chapters and that basically, Agatha didn’t want her to live in Camelot with them, and to make Agatha look like less of a dick Soman our dear author decides to randomly bring Hort back to Sophie... now don't get me wrong that's great but um if Yuba knew he wasn't dead she could have told Sophie instead of making her suffer. Anyways I just thought Sophie deserved a lot better in this book. it came to the point that I just rather have a sad ending, where she realizes shes not supposed to have love and walks into the ocean and disappears like a myth. Or becomes queen of something. I just thought Soman was a bit unfair handing out endings. Tedros wasn’t as bad in this book which was a nice change. Some of the deaths seemed pointless like when you kill off so many people that it just loses its dramatic effect. This book would have been a lot better if only (Robin, Guinevere, and Hort) died. The Nicola rebound thing was also stupid Soman a kpop star? hophie wasn't that cute either.<br />Lastly, the ending seemed rushed and only Agatha and Tedros got a clear ending.</span>

<div id="review_3134653827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3134653827" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56528294-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539285886p2/56528294.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3134653827?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/56528294-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/54083584-one-true-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56528294-jasmine?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56528294-jasmine?shelf=disappointing-sequel">disappointing-sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56528294-jasmine?shelf=most-anticipated-2020">most-anticipated-2020</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3134653827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13123998711545491580"><b> 2.5 stars</b><br/>In all honesty, my first thought after just finishing this that I feel betrayed. I'll be honest, I'm just going to pretend that the last three books don't exist and that I didn't read them. Would I read anything else written in this world in the future? Probably yes but I stick with what I've said.<br/><br/>Here's why I feel this way:<br/>1) A lot of the plot points in the last book seem so convenient. My problem with this is that I don't feel like everything ties back into the original trilogy very </span>
  <span id="freeText13123998711545491580" style="display:none"><b> 2.5 stars</b><br />In all honesty, my first thought after just finishing this that I feel betrayed. I'll be honest, I'm just going to pretend that the last three books don't exist and that I didn't read them. Would I read anything else written in this world in the future? Probably yes but I stick with what I've said.<br /><br />Here's why I feel this way:<br />1) A lot of the plot points in the last book seem so convenient. My problem with this is that I don't feel like everything ties back into the original trilogy very well.<br /><br /> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ One example is Arthur's 'true' heir...umm...Okay but that was a pretty bland and undeveloped character about whom we know pretty much nothing but fine. Would it be more interesting if he'd been alive and the one fighting Tedros...100% yes. Similarly, it was interesting when Japeth was Arthur's son. Good people can give birth to bad people and it could be vice versa. Japeth was actually interesting in book 5 but this wasn't the case in here. He was so cliche bad that it hurt. <br /><br />Here's a sentence about Andail and Hester being a relationship. Ummm....since when? Why am I being told this and not shown? How and when did they start dating? I feel like I'm losing context for this. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />Maybe this because, it's been a while since I last read the books or maybe it's the nostalgia of the first trilogy but I just don't think that the plot links back into the original trilogy very well. <br /><br />2) The characters- I'm not a huge of Tedros in this trilogy which is ironic because it's meant to be <i> his</i> trilogy. I remember liking him in the original trilogy but in the Camelot years it just feels like all he does is whine. He's just not very interesting in my opinion. I love Agatha and Sophie and I wanted a bigger focus on them so I'm complaining about the way Tedros is presented because he felt annoying and I didn't connect to him a lot. <br /><br />But! There were some great Sophie moments in this that I loved. Sophie might be my favourite character. <br /><br />4) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The ending- I don't like the ship Hort x Sophie. I liked the fact that Sophie's happy ending was her realising she didn't need a prince but herself. I like Hort but I don't like him with Sophie as a couple and I just didn't like that convenient happy ending for them. In fact, I was so disconnected to the story by the end that I didn't care about Merlin's death. Merlin's death! That just proves how disconnected I was. I love Merlin and I didn't care.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />So overall, it didn't feel like the end of ends for this series and I'm going to pretend the last three books never happened. I liked parts of it but disliked large chunks of it and hence my rating of 2.5 stars feels perfect. I would someday like to reread the whole series to see if my opinion changes but for now...I'm sticking with up to book 3 and forgetting I ever read the second trilogy. Despite all this, I'm intrigued to see what Chainani comes up with next.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3013288431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11672926700701825073">WOW. It's been a long time since I've given a book a five star rating. This book was simply perfect. I enjoyed this journey so much. The writing and storyline was so exciting and captivating. That's a lot coming from a 35 year old woman. I can't wait for the Netflix series!<br/><br/>UPDATE: 10/14/2020<br/>I felt I needed to add a bit more detail to this review so that I can look back and reflect on why I loved this book so much. One of the main reasons was that I could really relate to Agatha. She is such a st</span>
  <span id="freeText11672926700701825073" style="display:none">WOW. It's been a long time since I've given a book a five star rating. This book was simply perfect. I enjoyed this journey so much. The writing and storyline was so exciting and captivating. That's a lot coming from a 35 year old woman. I can't wait for the Netflix series!<br /><br />UPDATE: 10/14/2020<br />I felt I needed to add a bit more detail to this review so that I can look back and reflect on why I loved this book so much. One of the main reasons was that I could really relate to Agatha. She is such a strong willed, independent and fierce female. That causes her to be very dominant in everything that she does; which annoyed Tedros to no end. I saw the struggle she and Tedros went through in their relationship because , to him, she didnt let him truly be the "man" in their relationship. She loved so passionately and fiercely that she would do ANYTHING to make sure those around her were safe. I loved how she never backed down and never conformed. She was confident, brave and smart. Many men tend to shy away from females like that. I know that thought ran through Tedros's mind on many occasions. However, I love how Tedros was able to recognize those traits in her, and although I know it was hard for him, he truly accepted and loved her. I love that this was displayed in a middle grade book because it sends a powerful message to young ladies. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11672926700701825073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Lulu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88321281-lulu"><img alt="Lulu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605477942p2/88321281.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3413841874?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lulu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lulu" href="/user/show/88321281-lulu">Lulu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88321281-lulu?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88321281-lulu?shelf=this-book-made-me-angry">this-book-made-me-angry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88321281-lulu?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88321281-lulu?shelf=this-book-was-disappointing">this-book-was-disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/88321281-lulu?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3413841874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10238435915851855419">SGE has been one of my favorite series for years, but this story was such a lackluster final installment. The book is overly long, but it also reads like a rushed draft, complete with exposition-heavy dialogue and odd pacing. Random backstories, character relationships, and twists come out of nowhere; they often feel unplanned and pointless. <br/><br/>The book also has some weirdly sexist themes?? Its understanding of feminism is dated. It’s really a bummer, because other books in the series do a great jo</span>
  <span id="freeText10238435915851855419" style="display:none">SGE has been one of my favorite series for years, but this story was such a lackluster final installment. The book is overly long, but it also reads like a rushed draft, complete with exposition-heavy dialogue and odd pacing. Random backstories, character relationships, and twists come out of nowhere; they often feel unplanned and pointless. <br /><br />The book also has some weirdly sexist themes?? Its understanding of feminism is dated. It’s really a bummer, because other books in the series do a great job at exploring gender roles in the context of fairytales. The depiction of Dot also felt fat-phobic and needlessly mean, at times. <br /><br />Sophie was great, though! Nic deserves better, and Tedros still stinks. <br /><br />(If you love this series, like I do, I really recommend just sticking with the first trilogy.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10238435915851855419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J/6MAVomAgGQIQBhrJ1bYnK7FOH7I6iYrOBnzLKsP3KltBVP9asst8MQIkzaxyJDwHrgI8oJkGhS1o7WRSuZcg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('S05GodQKlDMK++M8laYNTXUyvFW5TorFgOJsP4ODlDnJBN/ve4e6hVnKwRHj/HRsx/NIl4hksjV+1IUldAQyOQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer4536591860490637408">Soman Chainani's first novel, THE SCHOOL FOR GOOD AND EVIL, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List, has been translated into 26 languages across six continents, and will soon be a major motion picture from Universal Studios. <br/><br/>The sequels, A WORLD WITHOUT PRINCES and THE LAST EVER AFTER, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List as well. Together, the books of the series have been on the </span>
  <span id="freeText4536591860490637408" style="display:none">Soman Chainani's first novel, THE SCHOOL FOR GOOD AND EVIL, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List, has been translated into 26 languages across six continents, and will soon be a major motion picture from Universal Studios. <br /><br />The sequels, A WORLD WITHOUT PRINCES and THE LAST EVER AFTER, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List as well. Together, the books of the series have been on the print and extended NYT lists for a total of 33 weeks.<br /><br />As a writer and film director, Soman's films have played at over 150 film festivals around the world, winning more than 30 jury and audience prizes, and his writing awards include honors from Big Bear Lake, New Draft, the CAPE Foundation, the Sun Valley Writer’s Fellowship, and the coveted Shasha Grant, awarded by a jury of international film executives. <br /><br />When he’s not telling stories or teaching in New York City, Soman is a die-hard tennis player who never lost a first-round match for ten years . . . until he started writing THE SCHOOL FOR GOOD AND EVIL. Now he loses all the time.<br /></span>
